</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar" style="padding-top:0;"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Bengalis" title="Template:Bengalis"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Bengalis" title="Template talk:Bengalis"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Bengalis&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Bengali</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">ben-<span style="font-size:90%">GAW</span>-lee</i></a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> generally known by its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">endonym</a> <b>Bangla</b> (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">বাংলা</span></span>, <small>Bengali pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" lang="bn-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Bengali" title="Help:IPA/Bengali">[ˈbaŋla]</a></span>), is an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan language</a> native to the <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> region of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. It is the official, national, and most widely spoken language of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and the second most widely spoken of the 22 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scheduled_languages_of_India" title="Scheduled languages of India">scheduled languages of India</a>. With approximately 300 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_speakers" title="Native speakers">native speakers</a> and another 37 million as <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">second language</a> speakers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnologue_ben_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue_ben-1">[1]</a></sup> Bengali is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">fifth most-spoken native language</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_total_number_of_speakers" title="List of languages by total number of speakers">seventh most spoken language</a> by total number of speakers in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Bengali is the fifth most spoken Indo-European language.
</p><p>Bengali is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national language</a> of Bangladesh,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bengali_Act_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bengali_Act-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpedia_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpedia-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-11">[11]</a></sup> with 98% of <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis" title="Bangladeshis">Bangladeshis</a> using Bengali as their first language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Within India, Bengali is the official language of the states of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">Tripura</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Barak_Valley" title="Barak Valley">Barak Valley</a> region of the state of <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>. It is also a second official language of the Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a> since September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Avenue_Mail_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Avenue_Mail-4">[4]</a></sup> It is the most widely spoken language in the <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-14">[14]</a></sup> and is spoken by significant populations in other states including <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arunachal_Pradesh" title="Arunachal Pradesh">Arunachal Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chhattisgarh" title="Chhattisgarh">Chhattisgarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mizoram" title="Mizoram">Mizoram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagaland" title="Nagaland">Nagaland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand" title="Uttarakhand">Uttarakhand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-langminor_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-langminor-15">[15]</a></sup> Bengali is also spoken by the Bengali diasporas (<a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_diaspora" title="Bangladeshi diaspora">Bangladeshi diaspora</a> and Indian Bengalis) in Europe, the United States, the Middle East and other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bengali has developed over the course of more than 1,300 years. <a href="/wiki/Bengali_literature" title="Bengali literature">Bengali literature</a>, with its millennium-old literary history, extensively developed during the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Renaissance" title="Bengali Renaissance">Bengali Renaissance</a> and is one of the most prolific and diverse literary traditions in Asia. The <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language_movement" title="Bengali language movement">Bengali language movement</a> from 1948 to 1956 demanding Bengali to be an official language of Pakistan fostered <a href="/wiki/Bengali_nationalism" title="Bengali nationalism">Bengali nationalism</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Bengal" title="East Bengal">East Bengal</a> leading to the emergence of Bangladesh in 1971. In 1999, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> recognised <a href="/wiki/Language_Movement_Day" title="Language Movement Day">21 February</a> as <a href="/wiki/International_Mother_Language_Day" title="International Mother Language Day">International Mother Language Day</a> in recognition of the language movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first native name for Bengali was <i>Gauda-bhasa</i> in 16th century. In the 19th century, it was known as <i>Vanga-bhasa</i> or <i>Bangala-bhasa</i>. In the 21st century, it is known as <i>Bangla-bhasa</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png/220px-Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png/330px-Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png/440px-Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indo-European_Language_Family_Branches_in_Eurasia.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Present-day distribution of Indo-European languages in Eurasia. Bengali belongs to easternmost spoken Indo-European language family</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="546" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG/220px-Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG/330px-Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG/440px-Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_indoiranias.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indo- Iranian language family, Bengali marked yellow</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:East-magadhan-proto-languages.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/East-magadhan-proto-languages.png/220px-East-magadhan-proto-languages.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/East-magadhan-proto-languages.png/330px-East-magadhan-proto-languages.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/East-magadhan-proto-languages.png/440px-East-magadhan-proto-languages.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:East-magadhan-proto-languages.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The descent of proto-Gauda, the ancestor of the modern Bengali language, from the proto-Gauda-Kamarupa line of the proto-Magadhan(Magadhi Prakrit).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> was practised by Hindu <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brahmins" title="Brahmins">Brahmins</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_millennium_BCE" title="First millennium BCE">first millennium BCE</a>, the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> population were speaking in some varieties of the <a href="/wiki/Prakrit" title="Prakrit">Prakrit</a>. These varieties generally referred to as "eastern <a href="/wiki/Magadhi_Prakrit" title="Magadhi Prakrit">Magadhi Prakrit</a>", as coined by linguist <a href="/wiki/Suniti_Kumar_Chatterji" title="Suniti Kumar Chatterji">Suniti Kumar Chatterji</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Middle Indo-Aryan languages">Middle Indo-Aryan dialects</a> were influential in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_millennium" title="First millennium">first millennium</a> when Bengal was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadhan</a> realm.
</p><p>The local varieties had no official status during the <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">Gupta Empire</a>, and with Bengal increasingly becoming a hub of <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit_literature" title="Sanskrit literature">Sanskrit literature</a> for Hindu priests, the vernacular of Bengal gained a lot of influence from Sanskrit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Magadhi_Prakrit" title="Magadhi Prakrit">Magadhi Prakrit</a> was also spoken in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>, and this vernacular eventually evolved into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ardha_Magadhi" title="Ardha Magadhi">Ardha Magadhi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jain_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-jain-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keith_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-keith-23">[23]</a></sup> Ardha Magadhi began to give way to what is known as <a href="/wiki/Apabhra%E1%B9%83%C5%9Ba" title="Apabhraṃśa">Apabhraṃśa</a>, by the end of the first millennium. The Bengali language evolved as a distinct language over the course of time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tb_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-tb-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early">Early</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Though some archeologists claim that some 10th-century texts were in Bengali, it is not certain whether they represent a differentiated language or whether they represent a stage when <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Eastern Indo-Aryan languages">Eastern Indo-Aryan languages</a> were differentiating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The local Apabhraṃśa of the eastern subcontinent, Purbi Apabhraṃśa or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abahatta" title="Abahatta">Abahatta</a> (lit. 'meaningless sounds'), eventually evolved into regional dialects, which in turn formed three groups, the <a href="/wiki/Bengali%E2%80%93Assamese_languages" title="Bengali–Assamese languages">Bengali–Assamese languages</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bihari_languages" title="Bihari languages">Bihari languages</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Odia_language" title="Odia language">Odia language</a>. The language was not static: different varieties coexisted and authors often wrote in multiple dialects in this period. For example, Ardhamagadhi is believed to have evolved into Abahatta around the 6th century, which competed with the ancestor of Bengali for some time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abahatta_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-abahatta-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The ancestor of Bengali was the language of the <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pala Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sena_dynasty" title="Sena dynasty">Sena dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">Medieval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Medieval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Persian_language_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="Persian language in the Indian subcontinent">Persian language in the Indian subcontinent</a></div><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="814" data-file-width="1614" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg/220px-Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg/330px-Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg/440px-Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silver_coin_of_Danujamarddana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Silver coin of Maharaj Gaudeshwar Danujmardandev of <a href="/wiki/Deva_dynasty" title="Deva dynasty">Deva dynasty</a>, circa 1417</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1241" data-file-width="1241" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG/220px-Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG/330px-Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG/440px-Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coin_-_Silver_-_Circa_9-10th_Century_13th_Century_CE_-_Harikela_Kingdom_-_ACCN_90-C2752_-_Indian_Museum_-_Kolkata_2014-04-04_4303.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Silver coin with proto-Bengali script, <a href="/wiki/Harikela" title="Harikela">Harikela</a> Kingdom, circa 9th–13th century</div></div></div>
<p>During the medieval period, Middle Bengali was characterised by the <a href="/wiki/Elision" title="Elision">elision</a> of word-final <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">অ</span></span> <i>ô</i>, the spread of compound verbs, and influence from the <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farsi" title="Farsi">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic languages</a>. The arrival of merchants and traders from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkestan" title="Turkestan">Turkestan</a> into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a>-ruling <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pala Empire</a>, from as early as the 7th century, gave birth to Islamic influence in the region. In the 13th century, the subsequent Muslim expeditions to Bengal greatly encouraged the migratory movements of <a href="/wiki/Arab_Muslims" title="Arab Muslims">Arab Muslims</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turco-Persian_tradition" title="Turco-Persian tradition">Turco-Persians</a>, who heavily influenced the local vernacular by settling among the native population.
</p><p>Bengali acquired prominence, over Persian, in the court of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultans_of_Bengal" title="Sultans of Bengal">Sultans of Bengal</a> with the ascent of <a href="/wiki/Jalaluddin_Muhammad_Shah" title="Jalaluddin Muhammad Shah">Jalaluddin Muhammad Shah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Subsequent Muslim rulers actively promoted the literary development of Bengali,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> allowing it to become the most spoken <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a> language in the Sultanate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEaton1993_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEaton1993-31">[31]</a></sup> Bengali adopted many words from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, which was a manifestation of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_culture" title="Islamic culture">Islamic culture</a> on the language. Major texts of Middle Bengali (1400–1800) include <a href="/wiki/Yusuf-Zulekha" title="Yusuf-Zulekha">Yusuf-Zulekha</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shah_Muhammad_Sagir" title="Shah Muhammad Sagir">Shah Muhammad Sagir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shreekrishna_Kirtana" title="Shreekrishna Kirtana">Shreekrishna Kirtana</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Chandidas" title="Chandidas">Chandidas</a> poets. Court support for Bengali culture and language waned when the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> conquered Bengal in the late 16th and early 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language_movement" title="Bengali language movement">Bengali language movement</a></div>
<p>The modern literary form of Bengali was developed during the 19th and early 20th centuries based on the dialect spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Nadia_district" title="Nadia district">Nadia region</a>, a west-central Bengali dialect. Bengali presents a strong case of <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">diglossia</a>, with the literary and standard form differing greatly from the colloquial speech of the regions that identify with the language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cornell_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-cornell-33">[33]</a></sup> The modern <a href="/wiki/Bengali_vocabulary" title="Bengali vocabulary">Bengali vocabulary</a> contains the vocabulary base from Magadhi Prakrit and Pali, also <a href="/wiki/Tatsama" title="Tatsama">tatsamas</a> and reborrowings from Sanskrit and other major borrowings from <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic languages</a> and other languages in contact with.
</p><p>During this period, there were two main forms of written Bengali:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">চলিতভাষা</span></span> <i>Chôlitôbhasha</i>; colloquial form of Bengali using simplified inflections</li>
<li><span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">সাধুভাষা</span></span> <i><a href="/wiki/Sadhu_bhasha" title="Sadhu bhasha">Sadhubhasha</a></i>; Sanskritised form of Bengali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SKumar_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-SKumar-34">[34]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In 1948, the Government of Pakistan tried to impose <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> as the sole state language in Pakistan, starting the Bengali language movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sas_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-sas-35">[35]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengali_Language_Movement" title="Bengali Language Movement">Bengali Language Movement</a> was a popular ethno-linguistic movement in the former <a href="/wiki/East_Bengal" title="East Bengal">East Bengal</a> (today <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>), which was a result of the strong linguistic consciousness of the <a href="/wiki/Bengalis" title="Bengalis">Bengalis</a> to gain and protect spoken and written Bengali's recognition as a state language of the then <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan" title="Dominion of Pakistan">Dominion of Pakistan</a>. On 21 February 1952, five students and political activists were killed during protests near the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dhaka" title="University of Dhaka">University of Dhaka</a>, whom were the first ever <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martyrs" title="Martyrs">Martyrs</a> to die for their rights on speaking their mother language. In 1956, Bengali was made a state language of Pakistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sas_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-sas-35">[35]</a></sup> The day has since been observed as <a href="/wiki/Language_Movement_Day" title="Language Movement Day">Language Movement Day</a> in Bangladesh and is also commemorated as <a href="/wiki/International_Mother_Language_Day" title="International Mother Language Day">International Mother Language Day</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> every year since 2000.
</p><p>In 2010, the parliament of Bangladesh and the legislative assembly of West Bengal proposed that Bengali be made an official <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> language,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-36">[36]</a></sup> though no further action was taken on this matter.
</p>

1.5x, Bengal</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_distribution">Geographical distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geographical distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg/250px-Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg/375px-Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg/500px-Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamtramck_Bangladeshi_mural.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A mural with Bengali letters in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamtramck" title="Hamtramck">Hamtramck</a>-<a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, United States</div></div></div>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div class="mw-no-invert" style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black;transform:scaleX(-1)rotate(-90deg)">
<div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:#a5a5a5"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 1057.8894993406px; border-left-color:#ffc000"></div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Approximate distribution of native Bengali speakers (assuming a rounded total of 261 million) worldwide.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#5b9bd5; color:black;"> </span> Bangladesh (61.3%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffc000; color:black;"> </span> India (37.2%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#a5a5a5; color:black;"> </span> Other (1.5%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>The Bengali language is native to the region of <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a>, which comprises the present-day nation of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and the Indian state of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>.
</p><p>Besides the native region it is also spoken by the Bengalis living in <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">Tripura</a>, southern <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and the Bengali population in the Indian union territory of <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a>. Bengali is also spoken in the neighbouring states of <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>, and sizeable minorities of Bengali speakers reside in Indian cities outside Bengal, including <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thane" title="Thane">Thane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a>. There are also significant Bengali-speaking communities in the <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis_in_the_Middle_East" title="Bangladeshis in the Middle East">Middle East</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengali_American" title="Bengali American">United States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis_in_Malaysia" title="Bangladeshis in Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangladeshis_in_Australia" title="Bangladeshis in Australia">Australia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_Canadian" title="Bangladeshi Canadian">Canada</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Bangladeshi" title="British Bangladeshi">United Kingdom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis_in_Italy" title="Bangladeshis in Italy">Italy</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_status">Official status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Official status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/States_of_India_by_Bengali_speakers" title="States of India by Bengali speakers">States of India by Bengali speakers</a></div>
<p>The 3rd article of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Constitution of Bangladesh">Constitution of Bangladesh</a> states Bengali to be the sole <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-11">[11]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangla_Bhasha_Prachalan_Ain,_1987" title="Bangla Bhasha Prachalan Ain, 1987">Bengali Language Implementation Act, 1987</a> made it mandatory to use Bengali in all records and correspondences, laws, proceedings of court and other legal actions in all courts, government or semi-government offices, and autonomous institutions in Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bengali_Act_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bengali_Act-9">[9]</a></sup> It is also the <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national</a> language of the country.
</p><p>In India, Bengali is one of the 23 <a href="/wiki/Languages_with_official_status_in_India" title="Languages with official status in India">official languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secondmost_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-secondmost-42">[42]</a></sup> It is the official language of the Indian states of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">Tripura</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Barak_Valley" title="Barak Valley">Barak Valley</a> of <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Bengali has been a second official language of the <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">Indian state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a> since September 2011.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, Bengali is a recognised secondary language in the city of <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The Department of Bengali in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Karachi" title="University of Karachi">University of Karachi</a> also offers regular programs of studies at the Bachelors and at the Masters levels for Bengali Literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>The national anthems of both Bangladesh (<i><a href="/wiki/Amar_Sonar_Bangla" title="Amar Sonar Bangla">Amar Sonar Bangla</a></i>) and India (<i><a href="/wiki/Jana_Gana_Mana" title="Jana Gana Mana">Jana Gana Mana</a></i>) were written in Bengali by the Bengali Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Additionally, the first two verses of <i><a href="/wiki/Vande_Mataram" title="Vande Mataram">Vande Mataram</a></i>, a patriotic song written in Bengali by <a href="/wiki/Bankim_Chandra_Chatterjee" title="Bankim Chandra Chatterjee">Bankim Chandra Chatterjee</a>, was adopted as the "national song" of India in both the colonial period and later in 1950 in independent India. Furthermore, it is believed by many that the national anthem of Sri Lanka (<a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Matha" title="Sri Lanka Matha">Sri Lanka Matha</a>) was inspired by a Bengali poem written by <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI030411_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOI030411-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TH040216_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-TH040216-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HT120510_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-HT120510-53">[53]</a></sup> while some even believe the anthem was originally written in Bengali and then translated into <a href="/wiki/Sinhala_language" title="Sinhala language">Sinhala</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wickramasinghe_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wickramasinghe-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM300315_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-DM300315-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS070511_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS070511-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TH170511_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-TH170511-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the contribution made by the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_UN_Peacekeeping_Force" title="Bangladesh UN Peacekeeping Force">Bangladesh UN Peacekeeping Force</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a> under the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Sierra_Leone" title="United Nations Mission in Sierra Leone">United Nations Mission in Sierra Leone</a>, the government of <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Ahmad Tejan Kabbah</a> declared Bengali as an honorary official language in December 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, elected representatives in both Bangladesh and West Bengal called for Bengali to be made an <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_the_United_Nations" title="Official languages of the United Nations">official language of the United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dialects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_dialects" title="Bengali dialects">Bengali dialects</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1250" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg/300px-Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg/450px-Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg/600px-Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bengali_dialects_political_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> (and some districts of <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>) which shows the <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> of the Bengali language. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:yellow; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bengali" title="Eastern Bengali">Eastern Bengali</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff8080; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Manbhumi_dialect" title="Manbhumi dialect">Manbhumi dialect</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:blue; color:white;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Varendri_dialect" title="Varendri dialect">Varendri dialect</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:red; color:black;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rarhi_dialect" title="Rarhi dialect">Rarhi dialect</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:maroon; color:white;"> </span> Sundarbani dialect</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#7c7cfc; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/KRNB_lects" title="KRNB lects">Rajbanshi dialect/language</a>*</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:green; color:white;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Chittagonian_language" title="Chittagonian language">Chittagonian dialect/language</a>*</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:orange; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Sylheti_language" title="Sylheti language">Sylheti dialect/language</a>*</div> (<i>those marked with an asterisk * are sometimes considered dialects or sometimes as separate languages</i>)</div></div></div>
<p>Regional variation in spoken Bengali constitutes a <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a>. Linguist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suniti_Kumar_Chattopadhyay" title="Suniti Kumar Chattopadhyay">Suniti Kumar Chattopadhyay</a> grouped the dialects of the eastern Magadhan languages into four large clusters that included Assamese and Odia – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rarhi_dialect" title="Rarhi dialect">Rarhi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangali_dialect" title="Bangali dialect">Vangiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kamarupi_Prakrit" title="Kamarupi Prakrit">Kamrupi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Varendri_dialect" title="Varendri dialect">Varendri</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> but many alternative grouping schemes have also been proposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morshed_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-morshed-65">[65]</a></sup> The south-western dialects (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rarhi_dialect" title="Rarhi dialect">Rarhi</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nadia_district" title="Nadia district">Nadia</a> dialect) form the basis of modern standard colloquial Bengali. In the dialects prevalent in much of eastern and south-eastern Bangladesh (<a href="/wiki/Barisal_Division" title="Barisal Division">Barisal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Division" title="Chittagong Division">Chittagong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dhaka_Division" title="Dhaka Division">Dhaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sylhet_Division" title="Sylhet Division">Sylhet Divisions</a> of Bangladesh), many of the stops and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">affricates</a> heard in <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> are pronounced as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">fricatives</a>. Western <a href="/wiki/Alveolo-palatal_consonant" title="Alveolo-palatal consonant">alveolo-palatal affricates</a> <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">চ</span></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal affricate">tɕɔ</a>]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ছ</span></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[<a href="/wiki/Aspirated_consonant" title="Aspirated consonant">tɕʰɔ</a>]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">জ</span></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal affricate">dʑɔ</a>]</span> correspond to eastern <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">চ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tsɔ]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ছ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tsʰɔ~sɔ]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">জ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[dzɔ~zɔ]</span>. The influence of <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">Tibeto-Burman languages</a> on the phonology of Eastern Bengali is seen through the lack of nasalised vowels and an alveolar articulation of what are categorised as the "cerebral" consonants (as opposed to the postalveolar articulation of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>). Some variants of Bengali, particularly <a href="/wiki/Chittagonian_language" title="Chittagonian language">Chittagonian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chakma_language" title="Chakma language">Chakma</a>, have contrastive <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tone</a>; differences in the pitch of the speaker's voice can distinguish words. <a href="/wiki/Rangpuri_language" title="Rangpuri language">Rangpuri</a>, Kharia Thar and Mal Paharia are closely related to Western Bengali dialects, but are typically classified as separate languages. Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Hajong_language" title="Hajong language">Hajong</a> is considered a separate language, although it shares similarities to Northern Bengali dialects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hajong_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-hajong-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the standardisation of Bengali in the 19th century and early 20th century, the cultural centre of Bengal was in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, a city founded by the British. What is accepted as the standard form today in both West Bengal and Bangladesh is based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rarhi_dialect" title="Rarhi dialect">West-Central dialect</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nadia_District" title="Nadia District">Nadia District</a>, located next to the border of Bangladesh and 76 miles north of Kolkata.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daniul_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-daniul-67">[67]</a></sup> There are cases where speakers of Standard Bengali in <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> will use a different word from a speaker of Standard Bengali in Bangladesh, even though both words are of native Bengali descent. For example, the word <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> is <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">নুন</span></span> <i>nun</i> in the west which corresponds to <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">লবণ</span></span> <i>lôbôṇ</i> in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banglabetelco_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Banglabetelco-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bengali exhibits <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">diglossia</a>, though some scholars have proposed triglossia or even n-glossia or <a href="/wiki/Heteroglossia" title="Heteroglossia">heteroglossia</a> between the written and spoken forms of the language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cornell_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-cornell-33">[33]</a></sup> Two styles of writing have emerged, involving somewhat different vocabularies and <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daniul_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-daniul-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daniul1_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-daniul1-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C4%81dhu_Bh%C4%81%E1%B9%A3%C4%81" title="Sādhu Bhāṣā">Shadhu-bhasha</a></i> (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">সাধু ভাষা</span></span> "uptight language") was the written language, with longer verb inflections and more of a <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>-derived <i><a href="/wiki/Tatsama" title="Tatsama">Tatsama</a></i> vocabulary. Songs such as India's national anthem <i><a href="/wiki/Jana_Gana_Mana" title="Jana Gana Mana">Jana Gana Mana</a></i> (by <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>) were composed in this style. Its use in modern writing however is uncommon, restricted to some official signs and documents in Bangladesh as well as for achieving particular literary effects.</li>
<li><i>Cholito-bhasha</i> (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">চলিত ভাষা</span></span> "running language"), known by linguists as Standard Colloquial Bengali, is a written Bengali style exhibiting a preponderance of colloquial idiom and shortened verb forms, and is the standard for written Bengali now. This form came into vogue towards the turn of the 19th century, promoted by the writings of <a href="/wiki/Peary_Chand_Mitra" title="Peary Chand Mitra">Peary Chand Mitra</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Alaler_Gharer_Dulal" title="Alaler Gharer Dulal">Alaler Gharer Dulal</a></i>, 1857),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alal_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-alal-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pramatha_Chaudhuri" title="Pramatha Chaudhuri">Pramatha Chaudhuri</a> (<i>Sabujpatra</i>, 1914) and in the later writings of <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>. It is modelled on the dialect spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Shantipur" title="Shantipur">Shantipur</a> region in <a href="/wiki/Nadia_district" title="Nadia district">Nadia district</a>, West Bengal. This form of Bengali is often referred to as the "Nadia standard", "Nadia dialect", "Southwestern/West-Central dialect" or "Shantipuri Bangla".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morshed_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-morshed-65">[65]</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>Linguist <a href="/wiki/Prabhat_Ranjan_Sarkar" title="Prabhat Ranjan Sarkar">Prabhat Ranjan Sarkar</a> categorises the language as:
</p>
<ul><li>Madhya <a href="/wiki/Rarh_region" title="Rarh region">Rarhi</a> dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Midnapore_district" title="Midnapore district">Kanthi</a> (Contai) dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kolkata_metropolitan_area" title="Kolkata metropolitan area">Kolkata</a> dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nadia_district" title="Nadia district">Shantipuriya</a> (Nadia) dialect</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shershahabadia" title="Shershahabadia">Shershahabadia</a> (Maldahiya/ Jangipuri) dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Varendra" title="Varendra">Barendri</a> dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rangpur_Division" title="Rangpur Division">Rangapuriya</a> dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sylhet_Division" title="Sylhet Division">Shrihatti</a> dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dhaka_Division" title="Dhaka Division">Dhakiya</a> (Bikrampuri) dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jessore_District" title="Jessore District">Jashore</a>/Jessoriya dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barisal_Division" title="Barisal Division">Barisal</a> (Chandradwip) dialect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Division" title="Chittagong Division">Chattal</a> (Chittagong) dialect</li></ul>
<p>While most writing is in Standard Colloquial Bengali (SCB), spoken dialects exhibit a greater variety. People in southeastern West Bengal, including Kolkata, speak in SCB. Other dialects, with minor variations from Standard Colloquial, are used in other parts of West Bengal and western Bangladesh, such as the <a href="/wiki/Midnapore" title="Midnapore">Midnapore</a> dialect, characterised by some unique words and constructions. However, a majority in Bangladesh speak in dialects notably different from SCB. Some dialects, particularly those of the <a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a> region, bear only a superficial resemblance to SCB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ray89_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-ray89-71">[71]</a></sup> The dialect in the Chittagong region is least widely understood by the general body of Bengalis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ray89_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-ray89-71">[71]</a></sup> The majority of Bengalis are able to communicate in more than one <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">variety</a> – often, speakers are fluent in <i>Cholitobhasha</i> (SCB) and one or more regional dialects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SKumar_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-SKumar-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even in SCB, the vocabulary may differ according to the speaker's religion: Muslims are more likely to use words of Persian and Arabic origin, along with more words naturally derived from Sanskrit (<a href="/wiki/Tadbhava" title="Tadbhava">tadbhava</a>), whereas Hindus are more likely to use <a href="/wiki/Tatsama" title="Tatsama">tatsama</a> (words directly borrowed from Sanskrit).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ray80_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-ray80-72">[72]</a></sup> For example:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banglabetelco_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Banglabetelco-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Phonology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_phonology" title="Bengali phonology">Bengali phonology</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemic</a> inventory of standard Bengali consists of 29 consonants and 7 vowels, as well as 7 <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">nasalised vowels</a>. The inventory is set out below in the <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">International Phonetic Alphabet</a> (upper grapheme in each box) and romanisation (lower grapheme).
</p>

<p>Bengali is known for its wide variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphthongs" title="Diphthongs">diphthongs</a>, combinations of <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowels</a> occurring within the same <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllable</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Two of these, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oi̯/</span> and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ou̯/</span>, are the only ones with representation in script, as <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ঐ</span></span> and <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ঔ</span></span> respectively. <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e̯ i̯ o̯ u̯/</span> may all form the glide part of a diphthong. The total number of diphthongs is not established, with bounds at 17 and 31. An incomplete chart is given by Sarkar (1985) of the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
