<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress">Stress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In standard Bengali, <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">stress</a> is predominantly initial. Bengali words are virtually all <a href="/wiki/Trochee" title="Trochee">trochaic</a>; the primary stress falls on the initial <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllable</a> of the word, while secondary stress often falls on all odd-numbered syllables thereafter, giving strings such as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">সহযোগিতা</span></span> <i><b>shô</b>-hô-<b>jo</b>-gi-<b>ta</b></i> "cooperation", where the <b>boldface</b> represents primary and secondary stress.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonant_clusters">Consonant clusters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Consonant clusters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_consonant_clusters" title="Bengali consonant clusters">Bengali consonant clusters</a></div>
<p>Native Bengali words do not allow initial <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">consonant clusters</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> the maximum syllabic structure is CVC (i.e. one vowel flanked by a consonant on each side). Many speakers of Bengali restrict their phonology to this pattern, even when using Sanskrit or English borrowings, such as <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">গেরাম</span></span> <i>geram</i> (CV.CVC) for <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">গ্রাম</span></span> <i>gram</i> (CCVC) "village" or <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ইস্কুল</span></span> <i>iskul</i> (VC.CVC) for <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">স্কুল</span></span> <i>skul</i> (CCVC) "school".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">Writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Writing system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengali-Assamese_Script" title="Bengali-Assamese Script">Bengali-Assamese Script</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali alphabet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Braille" title="Bengali Braille">Bengali Braille</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="354" decoding="async" height="416" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg/220px-Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg/330px-Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tagore_handwriting_Bengali.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of handwritten Bengali. Part of a poem written in Bengali (and with its English translation below each Bengali paragraph) by Nobel Laureate <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a> in 1926 in Hungary</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg/220px-Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg/330px-Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg/440px-Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bangla_lights_Whitechapel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Library of <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel" title="Whitechapel">Whitechapel</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_London" title="East London">East London</a> with the word "বাংলা" illuminated in its front.</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengali-Assamese_script" title="Bengali-Assamese script">Bengali-Assamese script</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Abugida" title="Abugida">abugida</a>, a script with letters for consonants, diacritics for vowels, and in which an <a href="/wiki/Inherent_vowel" title="Inherent vowel">inherent vowel</a> (অ <i>ô</i>) is assumed for consonants if no vowel is marked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-it46_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-it46-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali alphabet</a> is used throughout Bangladesh and eastern India (Assam, West Bengal, Tripura). The Bengali alphabet is believed to have evolved from a modified <a href="/wiki/Brahmic_scripts" title="Brahmic scripts">Brahmic script</a> around 1000 CE (or 10th–11th century).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akhor_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-akhor-78">[78]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Cursive" title="Cursive">cursive</a> script with eleven <a href="/wiki/Grapheme" title="Grapheme">graphemes</a> or signs denoting nine vowels and two <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a>, and thirty-nine graphemes representing <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">consonants</a> and other modifiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akhor_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-akhor-78">[78]</a></sup> There are no distinct <a href="/wiki/Letter_case" title="Letter case">upper and lower case</a> letter forms. The letters run from left to right and spaces are used to separate <a href="/wiki/Word#Orthography" title="Word">orthographic words</a>. Bengali script has a distinctive horizontal line running along the tops of the graphemes that links them together called <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মাত্রা</span></span> <i>matra</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the Bengali script is an abugida, its consonant graphemes usually do not represent phonetic <a href="/wiki/Segment_(linguistics)" title="Segment (linguistics)">segments</a>, but carry an "inherent" vowel and thus are <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllabic</a> in nature. The inherent vowel is usually a back vowel, either <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɔ]</span> as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মত</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[m<b>ɔ</b>t]</span> "opinion" or <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[o]</span>, as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মন</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[m<b>o</b>n]</span> "mind", with variants like the more open <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɒ]</span>. To emphatically represent a consonant sound without any inherent vowel attached to it, a special diacritic, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Virama" title="Virama">hôsôntô</a></i> <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">(্)</span></span>, may be added below the basic consonant grapheme (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ম্</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[m]</span>). This diacritic, however, is not common, and is chiefly employed as a guide to pronunciation. The abugida nature of Bengali consonant graphemes is not consistent, however. Often, syllable-final consonant graphemes, though not marked by a <i>hôsôntô</i>, may carry no inherent vowel sound (as in the final <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ন</span></span> in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মন</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[m<b>o</b>n]</span> or the medial <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ম</span></span> in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">গামলা</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡamla]</span>).
</p><p>A consonant sound followed by some vowel sound other than the inherent <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɔ]</span> is orthographically realised by using a variety of vowel <a href="/wiki/Allography" title="Allography">allographs</a> above, below, before, after, or around the consonant sign, thus forming the ubiquitous consonant-vowel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">typographic ligatures</a>. These allographs, called <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">কার</span></span> <i>kar</i>, are <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritical</a> vowel forms and cannot stand on their own. For example, the graph <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মি</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mi]</span> represents the consonant <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[m]</span> followed by the vowel <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i]</span>, where <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i]</span> is represented as the diacritical allograph<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ি</span></span> (called <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ই-কার</span></span> <i>i-kar</i>) and is placed <i>before</i> the default consonant sign. Similarly, the graphs <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মা</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ma]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মী</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mi]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মু</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mu]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মূ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mu]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মৃ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mri]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মে</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[me~mɛ]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মৈ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[moj]</span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মো</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mo]</span> and <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মৌ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mow]</span> represent the same consonant <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ম</span></span> combined with seven other vowels and two diphthongs. In these consonant-vowel ligatures, the so-called "inherent" vowel <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɔ]</span> is first expunged from the consonant before adding the vowel, but this intermediate expulsion of the inherent vowel is not indicated in any visual manner on the basic consonant sign <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ম</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mɔ]</span>.
</p><p>The vowel graphemes in Bengali can take two forms: the independent form found in the basic inventory of the script and the dependent, abridged, allograph form (as discussed above). To represent a vowel in isolation from any preceding or following consonant, the independent form of the vowel is used. For example, in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মই</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[moj]</span> "ladder" and in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ইলিশ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iliʃ]</span> "Hilsa fish", the independent form of the vowel <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ই</span></span> is used (cf. the dependent form<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ি)</span></span>. A vowel at the beginning of a word is always realised using its independent form.
</p><p>In addition to the inherent-vowel-suppressing <i>hôsôntô</i>, three more diacritics are commonly used in Bengali. These are the superposed <i>chôndrôbindu</i> <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">(ঁ)</span></span>, denoting a suprasegmental for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasalisation" title="Nasalisation">nasalisation</a> of vowels (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">চাঁদ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʃãd]</span> "moon"), the postposed <i>ônusbar</i> <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">(ং)</span></span> indicating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">velar nasal</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋ]</span> (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">বাংলা</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[baŋla]</span> "Bengali") and the postposed <i>bisôrgô</i> <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">(ঃ)</span></span> indicating the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">voiceless glottal fricative</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[h]</span> (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">উঃ!</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uh]</span> "ouch!") or the <a href="/wiki/Gemination" title="Gemination">gemination</a> of the following consonant (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">দুঃখ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[dukʰːɔ]</span> "sorrow").
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bengali_consonant_clusters" title="Bengali consonant clusters">Bengali consonant clusters</a> (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">যুক্তব্যঞ্জন</span></span> <i>juktôbênjôn</i>) are usually realised as ligatures, where the consonant which comes first is put on top of or to the left of the one that immediately follows. In these ligatures, the shapes of the constituent consonant signs are often contracted and sometimes even distorted beyond recognition. In the Bengali writing system, there are nearly 285 such ligatures denoting consonant clusters. Although there exist <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet#Consonant_conjuncts" title="Bengali alphabet">a few visual formulas</a> to construct some of these ligatures, many of them have to be learned by rote. Recently, in a bid to lessen this burden on young learners, efforts have been made by educational institutions in the two main Bengali-speaking regions (West Bengal and Bangladesh) to address the opaque nature of many consonant clusters, and as a result, modern Bengali textbooks are beginning to contain more and more "transparent" graphical forms of consonant clusters, in which the constituent consonants of a cluster are readily apparent from the graphical form. However, since this change is not as widespread and is not being followed as uniformly in the rest of the Bengali printed literature, today's Bengali-learning children will possibly have to learn to recognise both the new "transparent" and the old "opaque" forms, which ultimately amounts to an increase in learning burden.
</p><p>Bengali punctuation marks, apart from the downstroke <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">।</span></span> <i>daṛi</i> – the Bengali equivalent of a <a href="/wiki/Full_stop" title="Full stop">full stop</a> – have been adopted from western scripts and their usage is similar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike in western scripts (Latin, Cyrillic, etc.) where the letter-forms stand on an invisible baseline, the Bengali letter-forms instead hang from a visible horizontal left-to-right headstroke called <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">মাত্রা</span></span> <i>matra</i>. The presence and absence of this matra can be important. For example, the letter <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ত</span></span> <i>tô</i> and the numeral <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">৩</span></span> "3" are distinguishable only by the presence or absence of the <i>matra</i>, as is the case between the consonant cluster <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ত্র</span></span> <i>trô</i> and the independent vowel <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">এ</span></span> <i>e</i>. The letter-forms also employ the concepts of letter-width and letter-height (the vertical space between the visible matra and an invisible baseline).
</p><p>There is yet to be a uniform standard <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collating_sequence" title="Collating sequence">collating sequence</a> (sorting order of graphemes to be used in dictionaries, indices, computer sorting programs, etc.) of Bengali graphemes. Experts in both Bangladesh and India are currently working towards a common solution for this problem.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_and_historic_scripts">Alternative and historic scripts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Alternative and historic scripts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Halot-un-nabi-page1.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="264" decoding="async" height="358" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Halot-un-nabi-page1.gif/220px-Halot-un-nabi-page1.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d0/Halot-un-nabi-page1.gif 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Halot-un-nabi-page1.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An 1855 <a href="/wiki/Dobhashi" title="Dobhashi">Dobhashi</a> manuscript of <i>Halat-un-Nabi</i> written by <a href="/wiki/Sadeq_Ali" title="Sadeq Ali">Sadeq Ali</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Sylheti_Nagri" title="Sylheti Nagri">Sylheti Nagri</a> script.</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout history there have been instances of the Bengali language being written in different scripts, though these employments were never popular on a large scale and were communally limited. Owing to Bengal's geographic location, Bengali areas bordering non-Bengali regions have been influenced by each other. Small numbers of people in <a href="/wiki/Midnapore_district" title="Midnapore district">Midnapore</a>, which borders <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a>, have used the <a href="/wiki/Odia_script" title="Odia script">Odia script</a> to write in Bengali. In the border areas between <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, some Bengali communities historically wrote Bengali in <a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaithi" title="Kaithi">Kaithi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tirhuta_script" title="Tirhuta script">Tirhuta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChatterji1926234-235_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChatterji1926234-235-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Sylhet_Division" title="Sylhet Division">Sylhet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bankura_district" title="Bankura district">Bankura</a>, modified versions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaithi_script" title="Kaithi script">Kaithi script</a> had some historical prominence, mainly among Muslim communities. The variant in Sylhet was identical to the Baitali Kaithi script of <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">Hindustani</a> with the exception of Sylhet Nagri possessing <i>matra</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Sylhet Nagri was standardised for printing in <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1869</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpedia_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-bpedia-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Up until the 19th century, numerous variations of the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic script</a> had been used across Bengal from <a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a> in the east to <a href="/wiki/Meherpur_District" title="Meherpur District">Meherpur</a> in the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChatterji1926228–233_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChatterji1926228–233-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition of India</a> in the 20th century, the Pakistani government attempted to institute the Perso-Arabic script as the standard for Bengali in <a href="/wiki/East_Pakistan" title="East Pakistan">East Pakistan</a>; this was met with resistance and contributed to the Bengali language movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 16th century, Portuguese missionaries began a tradition of using the Roman alphabet to transcribe the Bengali language. Though the Portuguese-standard did not receive much growth, a few Roman Bengali works relating to Christianity and Bengali grammar were printed as far as <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> in 1743. The Portuguese were followed by the English and French respectively, whose works were mostly relating to Bengali grammar and transliteration. The first version of the <a href="/wiki/Aesop%27s_Fables" title="Aesop's Fables">Aesop's Fables</a> in Bengali was printed using Roman letters based on <a href="/wiki/English_phonology" title="English phonology">English phonology</a> by the Scottish linguist <a href="/wiki/John_Gilchrist_(linguist)" title="John Gilchrist (linguist)">John Gilchrist</a>. Consecutive attempts to establish a Roman Bengali has continued across every century since these times, and have been supported by the likes of <a href="/wiki/Suniti_Kumar_Chatterji" title="Suniti Kumar Chatterji">Suniti Kumar Chatterji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Qudrat-i-Khuda" title="Muhammad Qudrat-i-Khuda">Muhammad Qudrat-i-Khuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Enamul_Haq" title="Muhammad Enamul Haq">Muhammad Enamul Haq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChatterji1926233–234_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChatterji1926233–234-86">[86]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Digital_Revolution" title="Digital Revolution">Digital Revolution</a> has also played a part in the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/English_alphabet" title="English alphabet">English alphabet</a> to write Bengali,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> with certain social media influencers publishing entire novels in Roman Bengali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthographic_depth">Orthographic depth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Orthographic depth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Bengali script in general has a comparatively <a href="/wiki/Orthographic_depth" title="Orthographic depth">shallow orthography</a>, i.e., in most cases there is a one-to-one correspondence between the sounds (phonemes) and the letters (graphemes) of Bengali. But grapheme-phoneme inconsistencies do occur in certain cases.
</p><p>One kind of inconsistency is due to the presence of several letters in the script for the same sound. In spite of some modifications in the 19th century, the Bengali spelling system continues to be based on the one used for Sanskrit,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-63">[63]</a></sup> and thus does not take into account some sound mergers that have occurred in the spoken language. For example, there are three letters (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">শ</span></span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ষ</span></span>, and <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">স</span></span>) for the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">voiceless postalveolar fricative</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʃ]</span>, although the letter <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">স</span></span> retains the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant">voiceless alveolar sibilant</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[s]</span> sound when used in certain consonant conjuncts as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">স্খলন</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[skʰɔlon]</span> "fall", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">স্পন্দন</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[spɔndon]</span> "beat", etc. The letter <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ষ</span></span> also retains the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_sibilant" title="Voiceless retroflex sibilant">voiceless retroflex sibilant</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʂ]</span> sound when used in certain consonant conjuncts as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">কষ্ট</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kɔʂʈɔ]</span> "suffering", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">গোষ্ঠী</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡoʂʈʰi]</span> "clan", etc. Similarly, there are two letters (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">জ</span></span> and <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">য</span></span>) for the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_affricate" title="Voiced postalveolar affricate">voiced postalveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[dʒ]</span>. Moreover, what was once pronounced and written as a retroflex nasal <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ণ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɳ]</span> is now pronounced as an alveolar <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[n]</span> when in conversation (the difference is heard when reading) (unless conjoined with another <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_consonant" title="Retroflex consonant">retroflex consonant</a> such as <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ট</span></span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ঠ</span></span>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ড</span></span> and <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ঢ</span></span>), although the spelling does not reflect this change. The <a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">near-open front unrounded vowel</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[æ]</span> is orthographically realised by multiple means, as seen in the following examples: <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">এত</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[æto]</span> "so much", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">এ্যাকাডেমী</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ækademi]</span> "academy", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">অ্যামিবা</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[æmiba]</span> "amoeba", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">দেখা</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[dækʰa]</span> "to see", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ব্যস্ত</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[bæsto]</span> "busy", <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ব্যাকরণ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[bækorɔn]</span> "grammar".
</p><p>Another kind of inconsistency is concerned with the incomplete coverage of phonological information in the script. The inherent vowel attached to every consonant can be either <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɔ]</span> or <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[o]</span> depending on <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">vowel harmony</a> (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">স্বরসঙ্গতি</span></span>) with the preceding or following vowel or on the context, but this phonological information is not captured by the script, creating ambiguity for the reader. Furthermore, the inherent vowel is often not pronounced at the end of a syllable, as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">কম</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kɔm]</span> "less", but this omission is not generally reflected in the script, making it difficult for the new reader.
</p><p>Many consonant clusters have different sounds than their constituent consonants. For example, the combination of the consonants <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ক্</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[k]</span> and <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ষ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʂ]</span> is graphically realised as <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ক্ষ</span></span> and is pronounced <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kkʰo]</span> (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">রুক্ষ</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[rukkʰo]</span> "coarse"), <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kʰɔ]</span> (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ক্ষমতা</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kʰɔmota]</span> "capability") or even <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kʰo]</span> (as in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">ক্ষতি</span></span> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kʰoti]</span> "harm"), depending on the position of the cluster in a word. The Bengali writing system is, therefore, not always a true guide to pronunciation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The script used for Bengali, Assamese and other languages is known as <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali script</a>. The script is known as the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali alphabet</a> for Bengali and its dialects and the <a href="/wiki/Assamese_alphabet" title="Assamese alphabet">Assamese alphabet</a> for <a href="/wiki/Assamese_language" title="Assamese language">Assamese language</a> with some minor variations. Other related languages in the nearby region also make use of the Bengali script like the <a href="/wiki/Meitei_language" title="Meitei language">Meitei language</a> in the Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>, where the Meitei language has been written in the Bengali script for centuries, though the <a href="/wiki/Meitei_script" title="Meitei script">Meitei script</a> has been promoted in recent times.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Number_system">Number system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Number system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>There are additional digits for fractions and prices, though they are little used any longer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (August 2022)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanisation">Romanisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Romanisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romanisation_of_Bengali" title="Romanisation of Bengali">Romanisation of Bengali</a></div>
<p>There are various Romanisation systems used for Bengali created in recent years which have failed to represent the true Bengali phonetic sound. The Bengali alphabet has often been included with the group of Brahmic scripts for romanisation where the true phonetic value of Bengali is never represented. Some of them are the <a href="/wiki/International_Alphabet_of_Sanskrit_Transliteration" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration</a>, or IAST system (based on diacritics);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAST1_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-IAST1-89">[89]</a></sup> "Indian languages Transliteration", or <a href="/wiki/ITRANS" title="ITRANS">ITRANS</a> (uses upper case letters suited for <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a> keyboards);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ITRANS1_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-ITRANS1-90">[90]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_at_Kolkata_romanisation" title="National Library at Kolkata romanisation">National Library at Kolkata romanisation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatLib_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-NatLib-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the context of Bengali <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanisation" title="Romanisation">romanisation</a>, it is important to distinguish <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliteration</a> from <a href="/wiki/Transcription_(linguistics)" title="Transcription (linguistics)">transcription</a>. Transliteration is orthographically accurate (i.e. the original spelling can be recovered), whereas transcription is phonetically accurate (the pronunciation can be reproduced).
</p><p>Although it might be desirable to use a transliteration scheme where the original Bengali orthography is recoverable from the Latin text, Bengali words are currently Romanized on Wikipedia using a <a href="/wiki/Phonemic_orthography" title="Phonemic orthography">phonemic transcription</a>, where the true phonetic pronunciation of Bengali is represented with no reference to how it is written.
</p><p>The most recent attempt has been by publishers Mitra and Ghosh with the launch of three popular children's books, <i>Abol Tabol</i>, <i>Hasi Khusi</i> and <i>Sahoj Path</i> in Roman script at the Kolkata Book Fair 2018. Published under the imprint of Benglish Books, these are based on phonetic transliteration and closely follow spellings used in social media but for using an underline to describe soft consonants.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Grammar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_grammar" title="Bengali grammar">Bengali grammar</a></div>
<p>Bengali nouns are not assigned gender, which leads to minimal changing of adjectives (<a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflection</a>). However, nouns and pronouns are moderately <a href="/wiki/Declension" title="Declension">declined</a> (altered depending on their function in a sentence) into four <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">cases</a> while verbs are heavily <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_conjugation" title="Grammatical conjugation">conjugated</a>, and the verbs do not change form depending on the gender of the nouns.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Word order">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Head-directionality_parameter" title="Head-directionality parameter">head-final</a> language, Bengali follows a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93object%E2%80%93verb" title="Subject–object–verb">subject–object–verb</a> <a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">word order</a>, although variations on this theme are common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tb16_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-tb16-92">[92]</a></sup> Bengali makes use of <a href="/wiki/Preposition_and_postposition" title="Preposition and postposition">postpositions</a>, as opposed to the prepositions used in English and other European languages. <a href="/wiki/Determiner" title="Determiner">Determiners</a> follow the <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">noun</a>, while numerals, <a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">adjectives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Possession_(linguistics)" title="Possession (linguistics)">possessors</a> precede the noun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UCLA1_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA1-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Yes-no questions do not require any change to the basic word order; instead, the low (L) <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tone</a> of the final syllable in the utterance is replaced with a falling (HL) tone. Additionally, optional <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_particle" title="Grammatical particle">particles</a> (e.g. <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">কি</span></span> <i>-ki</i>, <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">না</span></span> <i>-na</i>, etc.) are often <a href="/wiki/Clitic" title="Clitic">encliticised</a> onto the first or last word of a yes-no question.
</p><p>Wh-questions are formed by fronting the wh-word to <a href="/wiki/Focus_(linguistics)" title="Focus (linguistics)">focus</a> position, which is typically the first or second word in the utterance.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">Nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Nouns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nouns and pronouns are inflected for <a href="/wiki/Declension" title="Declension">case</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Nominative_case" title="Nominative case">nominative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">objective</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive (possessive)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Locative_case" title="Locative case">locative</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tb_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-tb-24">[24]</a></sup> The case marking pattern for each noun being inflected depends on the noun's degree of <a href="/wiki/Animacy" title="Animacy">animacy</a>. When a <a href="/wiki/Article_(grammar)" title="Article (grammar)">definite article</a> such as <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">-টা</span></span> <i>-ṭa</i> (singular) or <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">-গুলো</span></span> <i>-gulo</i> (plural) is added, as in the tables below, nouns are also inflected for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a>.
</p><p>In most of the Bengali grammar books, cases are divided into 6 categories and an additional possessive case (possessive form is not recognised as a type of case by Bengali grammarians). But in terms of usages, cases are generally grouped into only 4 categories.
</p>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>When counted, nouns take one of a small set of <a href="/wiki/Measure_word" title="Measure word">measure words</a>. Nouns in Bengali cannot be counted by adding the numeral directly adjacent to the noun. An appropriate measure word (<b>MW</b>), a <a href="/wiki/Classifier_(linguistics)" title="Classifier (linguistics)">classifier</a>, must be used between the numeral and the noun (most languages of the <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia_linguistic_area" title="Mainland Southeast Asia linguistic area">Mainland Southeast Asia linguistic area</a> are similar in this respect). Most nouns take the generic measure word <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">-টা</span></span> <i>-ṭa</i>, though other measure words indicate semantic classes (e.g. <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">-জন</span></span> <i>-jôn</i> for humans). There is also the classifier <i>-khana,</i> and its diminutive form <i>-khani</i>, which attach only to nouns denoting something flat, long, square, or thin. These are the least common of the classifiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto">
<caption>Measure words
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Example
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">নয়<b>টা</b></p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Nôy-<b>ṭa</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">nine-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">গরু</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">goru</p><p style="margin: 0px;">cow</p></div><p style="display: none;">নয়<b>টা</b> গরু</p><p style="display: none;">Nôy-<b>ṭa</b> goru</p><p style="display: none;">nine-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b> cow</p><p style="clear: left;">Nine cows</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">কয়<b>টা</b></p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Kôy-<b>ṭa</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">how many-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">বালিশ</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">balish</p><p style="margin: 0px;">pillow</p></div><p style="display: none;">কয়<b>টা</b> বালিশ</p><p style="display: none;">Kôy-<b>ṭa</b> balish</p><p style="display: none;">{how many}-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b> pillow</p><p style="clear: left;">How many pillows</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">অনেক<b>জন</b></p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ônek-<b>jôn</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">many-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">লোক</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">lok</p><p style="margin: 0px;">person</p></div><p style="display: none;">অনেক<b>জন</b> লোক</p><p style="display: none;">Ônek-<b>jôn</b> lok</p><p style="display: none;">many-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b> person</p><p style="clear: left;">Many people</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">চার-পাঁচ<b>জন</b></p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ĉar-pãc-<b>jôn</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">four-five-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">শিক্ষক</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">shikkhôk</p><p style="margin: 0px;">teacher</p></div><p style="display: none;">চার-পাঁচ<b>জন</b> শিক্ষক</p><p style="display: none;">Ĉar-pãc-<b>jôn</b> shikkhôk</p><p style="display: none;">four-five-<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;" title="measure word">MW</abbr></b> teacher</p><p style="clear: left;">Four to five teachers</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Measuring nouns in Bengali without their corresponding measure words (e.g. <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">আট বিড়াল</span></span> <i>aṭ biṛal</i> instead of <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">আট<b>টা</b> বিড়াল</span></span> <i>aṭ-<b>ṭa</b> biṛal</i> "eight cats") would typically be considered ungrammatical. However, when the semantic class of the noun is understood from the measure word, the noun is often omitted and only the measure word is used, e.g. <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">শুধু এক<b>জন</b> থাকবে।</span></span> <i>Shudhu êk-<b>jôn</b> thakbe.</i> (lit. "Only one-<b>MW</b> will remain.") would be understood to mean "Only one <b>person</b> will remain.", given the semantic class implicit in <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">-জন</span></span> <i>-jôn</i>.
</p><p>In this sense, all nouns in Bengali, unlike most other Indo-European languages, are similar to <a href="/wiki/Mass_noun" title="Mass noun">mass nouns</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs">Verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Verbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are two classes of verbs: <a href="/wiki/Finite_verb" title="Finite verb">finite</a> and non-finite. Non-finite verbs have no inflection for tense or person, while finite verbs are fully inflected for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">person</a> (first, second, third), <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">tense</a> (present, past, future), <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">aspect</a> (simple, perfect, progressive), and <a href="/wiki/Honorific" title="Honorific">honour</a> (intimate, familiar, and formal), but <i>not</i> for number. <a href="/wiki/Conditional_mood" title="Conditional mood">Conditional</a>, imperative, and other special inflections for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">mood</a> can replace the tense and aspect suffixes. The number of inflections on many verb roots can total more than 200.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">Inflectional</a> suffixes in the <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphology</a> of Bengali vary from region to region, along with minor differences in <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a>.
</p><p>Bengali differs from most Indo-Aryan Languages in the <a href="/wiki/Zero_copula" title="Zero copula">zero copula</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Copula_(linguistics)" title="Copula (linguistics)">copula</a> or connective <i>be</i> is often missing in the present tense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-huq_sarkar-63">[63]</a></sup> Thus, "he is a teacher" is <span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">সে শিক্ষক</span></span> <i>se shikkhôk</i>, (literally "he teacher").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hacce-bangali_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-hacce-bangali-95">[95]</a></sup> In this respect, Bengali is similar to Russian and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>. <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> grammar is also the closest to Bengali grammar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hub1995_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-hub1995-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div class="mw-no-invert" style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black;transform:scaleX(-1)rotate(-90deg)">
<div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:brown"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 181.89932472811px; border-left-color:#d6722f"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:#d6722f"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:#d6722f"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:87.630668004386px 48.175367410172px 0 0; border-top-color:#2f75d6"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:#2f75d6"></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Sources of modern literary Bengali words
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#2f75d6; color:black;"> </span> Native (67%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#d6722f; color:black;"> </span> Sanskrit reborrowings (25%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:brown; color:white;"> </span> Indigenous and foreign loans (8%)</div>
</div>
</div></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_vocabulary" title="Bengali vocabulary">Bengali vocabulary</a></div>
<p>Bengali has as many as 100,000 separate words, of which 50,000 are considered <a href="/wiki/Tadbhava" title="Tadbhava">Tadbhavas</a>, 21,100 are <a href="/wiki/Tatsama" title="Tatsama">Tatsamas</a> and the remainder <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> from <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic</a> and other foreign languages.
</p><p>However, these figures do not take into account the large proportion of archaic or highly technical words that are very rarely used. Furthermore, different dialects use more <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> vocabulary especially in different areas of Bangladesh and Muslim majority areas of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>. Hindus, on the other hand, use more Sanskrit vocabulary than Muslims. Standard Bengali is based on the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_dialects" title="Bengali dialects">Nadia dialect</a> spoken in the Hindu majority states of West Bengal and parts of Muslim majority division of Khulna in Bangladesh. About 90% of Bengalis in Bangladesh (ca. 148 million) and 27% of Bengalis in West Bengal and 10% in Assam (ca. 36 million) are Muslim and the Bangladeshi Muslims and some of the Indian Bengali Muslims speak a more "persio-arabised" version of Bengali instead of the more Sanskrit influenced Standard <a href="/wiki/Bengali_dialects" title="Bengali dialects">Nadia dialect</a> although majority of the Indian Bengalis of West Bengal speaks in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rarhi_dialect" title="Rarhi dialect">Rarhi dialect</a> irrespective of religion. The productive vocabulary used in modern literary works, in fact, is made up mostly (67%) of tadbhavas, while tatsamas make up only 25% of the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhoumick_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-bhoumick-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhoumick1_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-bhoumick1-98">[98]</a></sup> Loanwords from non-Indic languages account for the remaining 8% of the vocabulary used in modern <a href="/wiki/Bengali_literature" title="Bengali literature">Bengali literature</a>.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Suniti_Kumar_Chatterji" title="Suniti Kumar Chatterji">Suniti Kumar Chatterji</a>, dictionaries from the early 20th century attributed about 50% of the Bengali vocabulary to native words (i.e., naturally modified <a href="/wiki/Prakrit" title="Prakrit">Prakrit</a> words, corrupted forms of <a href="/wiki/Aryan" title="Aryan">Aryan</a> words, and non-Indo-European languages). About 45% percent of Bengali words are unmodified Sanskrit, and the remaining words are from foreign languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-99">[99]</a></sup> Dominant in the last group was <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, which was also the source of some grammatical forms. More recent studies suggest that the use of native and foreign words has been increasing, mainly because of the preference of Bengali speakers for the colloquial style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-:02-99">[99]</a></sup> Because of centuries of contact with <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persians</a>, Bengali has absorbed numerous words from foreign languages, often totally integrating these borrowings into the core vocabulary.
</p><p>The most common borrowings from foreign languages come from three different kinds of contact. After close contact with several indigenous Austroasiatic languages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and later the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> invasion whose court language was Persian, numerous <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_language" title="Chagatai language">Chagatai</a>, Arabic, and Persian words were absorbed into the lexicon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sas_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-sas-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Later, East Asian travellers and lately European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a> brought words from <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, French, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, and most significantly English during the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">colonial period</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bengali_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sample text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following is a sample text in Bengali of Article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">সমস্ত</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Sômôstô</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ʃɔmosto</p><p style="margin: 0px;">All</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">মানুষ</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">manush</p><p style="margin: 0px;">manuʃ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">human</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">স্বাধীনভাবে</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">shadhinbhabe</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ʃadʱinbʱabe</p><p style="margin: 0px;">free-manner-in</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">সমান</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sôman</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ʃoman</p><p style="margin: 0px;">equal</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">মর্যাদা</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">môrjada</p><p style="margin: 0px;">mɔɾdʒada</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dignity</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">এবং</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ebông</p><p style="margin: 0px;">eboŋ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">and</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">অধিকার</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ôdhikar</p><p style="margin: 0px;">odʱikaɾ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">right</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">নিয়ে</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">niye</p><p style="margin: 0px;">nie̯e</p><p style="margin: 0px;">taken</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">জন্মগ্রহণ</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">jônmôgrôhôn</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dʒɔnmoɡrohon</p><p style="margin: 0px;">birth-take</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">করে।</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kôre.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">kɔɾe</p><p style="margin: 0px;">do.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">তাঁদের</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Tãder</p><p style="margin: 0px;">tãdeɾ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Their</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">বিবেক</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">bibek</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bibek</p><p style="margin: 0px;">reason</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">এবং</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ebông</p><p style="margin: 0px;">eboŋ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">and</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">বুদ্ধি</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">buddhi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">budʱːi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">intelligence</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">আছে;</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">achhe;</p><p style="margin: 0px;">atʃʰe</p><p style="margin: 0px;">exist;</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">সুতরাং</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sutôrang</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ʃutoraŋ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">therefore</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">সকলেরই</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sôkôleri</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ʃɔkoleɾi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">everyone-indeed</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">একে</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">êke</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ɛke</p><p style="margin: 0px;">one</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">অপরের</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ôpôrer</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ɔporeɾ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">another's</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">প্রতি</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">prôti</p><p style="margin: 0px;">proti</p><p style="margin: 0px;">towards</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">ভ্রাতৃত্বসুলভ</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">bhratrittôsulôbh</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bʱratritːoʃulɔbʱ</p><p style="margin: 0px;">brotherhood-ly</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">মনোভাব</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mônobhab</p><p style="margin: 0px;">monobʱab</p><p style="margin: 0px;">attitude</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">নিয়ে</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">niye</p><p style="margin: 0px;">nie̯e</p><p style="margin: 0px;">taken</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">আচরণ</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">achôrôn</p><p style="margin: 0px;">atʃorɔn</p><p style="margin: 0px;">conduct</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">করা</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kôra</p><p style="margin: 0px;">kɔra</p><p style="margin: 0px;">do</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bn" style="margin: 0px;">উচিত।</p><p lang="bn-Latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">uchit.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">utʃit</p><p style="margin: 0px;">should.</p></div><p style="display: none;">সমস্ত মানুষ স্বাধীনভাবে সমান মর্যাদা এবং অধিকার নিয়ে জন্মগ্রহণ করে। তাঁদের বিবেক এবং বুদ্ধি আছে; সুতরাং সকলেরই একে অপরের প্রতি ভ্রাতৃত্বসুলভ মনোভাব নিয়ে আচরণ করা উচিত।</p><p style="display: none;">Sômôstô manush shadhinbhabe sôman môrjada ebông ôdhikar niye jônmôgrôhôn kôre. Tãder bibek ebông buddhi achhe; sutôrang sôkôleri êke ôpôrer prôti bhratrittôsulôbh mônobhab niye achôrôn kôra uchit.</p><p style="display: none;">ʃɔmosto manuʃ ʃadʱinbʱabe ʃoman mɔɾdʒada eboŋ odʱikaɾ nie̯e dʒɔnmoɡrohon kɔɾe tãdeɾ bibek eboŋ budʱːi atʃʰe ʃutoraŋ ʃɔkoleɾi ɛke ɔporeɾ proti bʱratritːoʃulɔbʱ monobʱab nie̯e atʃorɔn kɔra utʃit</p><p style="display: none;">All human free-manner-in equal dignity and right taken birth-take do. Their reason and intelligence exist; therefore everyone-indeed one another's towards brotherhood-ly attitude taken conduct do should.</p><p style="clear: left;">All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They possess conscience and reason. Therefore, everyone should act in a spirit of brotherhood towards each other.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Within the Eastern Indic language family the history of the separation of Bangla from Odia, Assamese, and the languages of Bihar remains to be worked out carefully. Scholars do not yet agree on criteria for deciding if certain tenth century AD texts were in a Bangla already distinguishable from the other languages, or marked a stage at which Eastern Indic had not finished differentiating." (<a href="#CITEREFDasgupta2003">Dasgupta 2003</a>:386–387)</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"What is more significant, a contemporary Chinese traveler reported that although Persian was understood by some in the court, the language in universal use there was Bengali. This points to the waning, although certainly not yet the disappearance, of the sort of foreign mentality that the Muslim ruling class in Bengal had exhibited since its arrival over two centuries earlier. It also points to the survival, and now the triumph, of local Bengali culture at the highest level of official society." (<a href="#CITEREFEaton1993">Eaton 1993</a>:60)</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-huq_sarkar-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-huq_sarkar_63-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150706032246/http://en.banglapedia.org/index.php?title=Bangla_Language" rel="nofollow">"Bangla language"</a>. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://en.banglapedia.org/index.php?title=Bangla_Language" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on 6 July 2015.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Bangla+language&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fen.banglapedia.org%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DBangla_Language&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABengali+language"></span> in <a href="#CITEREFAsiatic_Society_of_Bangladesh2003">Asiatic Society of Bangladesh 2003</a></span>

<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-64">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Note that Chatterji's classification of 'Bengali dialects' includes lects ancestral to both Assamese and Odia. However, Chatterji does not intend to classify these lects as dialects of Bangla. Therefore, Chatterji's four dialects—Rāḍha, Varêndra, Vaŋga, and Kāmrupa—should not be termed 'dialects of Bengali' but rather, 'dialects [in the sense of historical
derivatives] of eastern Magadhan' (cf. Chatterji 1926:92ff.)." (<a href="#CITEREFToulmin2009">Toulmin 2009</a>:218)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-morshed-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-morshed_65-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-morshed_65-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFMorshed,_Abul_Kalam_Manjoor2012">Morshed, Abul Kalam Manjoor (2012). <a class="external text" href="http://en.banglapedia.org/index.php?title=Dialect" rel="nofollow">"Dialect"</a>. <li id="cite_note-hacce-bangali-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-hacce-bangali_95-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Among Bengali speakers brought up in neighbouring linguistic regions (e.g. Hindi), the lost copula may surface in utterances such as <i>she shikkhôk hocche</i>. This is viewed as ungrammatical by other speakers, and speakers of this variety are sometimes (humorously) referred as "hocche-Bangali".</span>
</li>
